< Review>
We came from abroad to the west coast for the Bald Eagles summer camp. Our kids spent their last six summers at the camp and convinced us to brave the pandemic, international border crossings, and airport restrictions. We flew across the Atlantic and the entire lower 48 to get here. Our oldest, Ethan, was a coach-in-training, a role he has been waiting for all year. Our daughter, Daphne, went to leadership camp, which she had been wanting to do for years. They made friends and had a chance to lead and run things. There is a strong focus on positive thinking and coach etiquette.

These were well spent two weeks. It was far from cheap for us parents, but it was well worth it. We are already thinking about next year.

Ohad and Yifat<//Review>

< review>
All around terrible shop. What started off friendly turned into a series of oops, I don't know and just a terrible experience.

First off, it is the law to provide a written estimate prior to doing any auto repair work in the State of California. While they did call me with an estimate, apparently they felt no need to honor it. Now on most things, cost can change a little, but on replacing a battery they spiked the cost almost a hundred bucks when I went to pick up the car, probably because they knew I wasn't doing any more work there. My battery had zero issues, nor did I have any electrical issues before coming here. They also charged me to diagnosis an AC recharge issue yet declined to fix the actual issue or even attempt to plug in one unplugged cord on the ac compressor, I've rectified this myself at this point and surprise, I did not need a new compressor.

Went to pick up the vehicle because after they changed the water pump I got an error for the alternator. My alternator was fine and had never given me any issues yet they swore it was not from their work and that I could pay around six hundred to replace it.

They had my car almost a week to repair an overheating issue. After I got it back I had to tighten lines to the power steering pump that had just been changed a month ago, still have an overheating issue as well as new transmission issues and a ton of fluid just all over my engine bay. (This had also been thoroughly cleaned after the last repair which was a hydraulic fan accuator.)

Will not be back here again, while they sincerely seemed to want to help, they could not figure my car out and seemed lost on basic details you can find on a repair forum most every time I spoke to them.

I went farther to show them twice exactly where the overheating issue was occuring, the thermostat housing unit, but they continued to offer to change hoses and other unrelated areas.

Not having time to do my own auto repair all the time I went here seeking an honest mechanic shop and found well, just a mess! Doing my own mechanic work so far on this vehicle fixed most issue they have screwed up but I will be seeking appropriate legal action against this shop of possible. Having never received a written estimate this should not be too difficult. In addition shop, you are welcome to issue me a full refund at any time as well.

Read through their existing reviews that originally were the reason I came here, they have a great reputation online. Wish I would have read them first though as most of them are very clearly fake, just another business buying fake reviews to look better than their service actually is.< /review>

< text>
Love the concept. The KoJa‚Äôs, as they‚Äôre called, have crispy garlic rice as the bun and are filled with meat or mushroom and topped with various toppings.  They also offer, and recommend pairing the KoJa with, waffle fries that are again loaded with meat and toppings.

I felt like the combination of KoJa and fries was way too much food.  I saw that they also offer ice cream sandwiches that look amazing, and I would have much rather tried one of those than eat the contents of a KoJa on top of waffle fries.  The KoJa (I had the original) was good and had great flavor combinations with the meat and toppings.  My only complaint is that once the toppings are consumed, you‚Äôre left with a somewhat monotonous flavor profile for the remaining 3/4 of the KoJa.< /text>

<text>This place was kind of a delicious surprise.
I passed by a couple of times and never thought to go in, it looks fancy but it‚Äôs actually nice and casual.

At first the menu is a little bit overwhelming. All of the items are fusion and if you‚Äôve never been there before can be a little overwhelming, that‚Äôs  remedied by some quick research and reading each item carefully. I‚Äôve included a screenshot of the menu to help that along before you go.

At a new lunch spot I generally like to start with whatever their famous dish is. In this case, The original KoJa  did it for me.
It‚Äôs a delicious mix of Korean short rib chopped lettuce wedged in between two disc shaped patties of rice. I must say the patties of rice or a little odd but fit the meal at least.

For a side dish I ordered the kamikaze fries which were awesome and worth every penny.
This is a great spot to take a risk and try for the first time. The food is delicious and neutral. Not too hot not too sweet not to, anything.   Just perfect.</text><UserId.>106373140847401106792< /UserId.><rate>4<//rate>< GmapID>

<Rating>5<//Rating><review>Now that Koja Kitchen has brick and mortar locations, everyone raves about them. In my best old grandmother voice: I remember when Koja Kitchen was just a food truck and I followed them around at all of the Moveable Feasts. ha ha! Well, the restaurants have a much larger menu, but the staples are still there. Gotta get the original short rib Koja 'burger' served on rice patty buns. Oh-their fries are criss cut style, and their special sauce is spicy for wimps like me.

For those of you who are not familiar with Koja Kitchen, what rock have you been hiding under? J/K It's Asian fusion that I'd say was made famous by their burgers served on rice patties instead of traditional bread. When you go to one of their restaurants, you order and pay for your food and they give you a bluetooth coaster that vibrates and lights up when your food is ready. Just chillax at a table until then. When your pager goes off, leave it on the counter and take your food. Don't forget to grab plasticware before you go eat.

Their expanded menu includes an assortment of bowls, including an ahi tuna bowl and a vegetarian option, called Teriyaki Zen Bowl, which comes with portobello mushroom, pineapple, green onions, & crispy shallots. They also serve tacos and salads now. If you're a fan of the fancy sodas, their fountain machine features Stubborn brand sodas.

This location on Brokaw and Old Oakland Road is huge. There are plenty of indoor and outdoor seating areas. They have heaters outside for those chilly days. Definitely an OG fan of Koja Kitchen and I am pleased to see so many people enjoying their food at the new restaurants.<//review></record></dataset><record>

<review>The wife had been to the Koja food truck back in the day at an Off The Grid event.  I guess the owner has gotten popular enough to be able to open a brick and mortar location.  This place is just down the street from my work.  So when I told her about it she got excited and wanted to stop by as she had liked her experience with the truck.

She recommended the Short Rib Koja for me.  So that's what we both ordered along with a chicken taco and an order of their Kamikaze fries to share.  I asked the cashier if their chicken was breast meat.  She went to the kitchen and asked one of the cooks if it was breast and he said "yes".  Our order was ready in about 5 minutes.  I went up to the counter to pick up the food, looked at the chicken taco and sure enough it looked like thigh meat.  I asked the cook if it was breast and he again said, "yes".  I figured that maybe the marinade made the meat look weird.  So I took it to the table and looked at it a bit harder and was convinced that it was thigh.

I start to get up to bring the taco back and I see a manager looking guy peering in my direction.  The cook must have talked to him about it because as soon as I walked up to him he apologized and said that the chicken was indeed thigh meat.  So I got a beef taco instead.  I don't know the manager's name but he was a cool looking Filipino guy with a septum piercing.  I meant to thank him for helping us out with the food when we left but he wasn't around at that time.

As for the food, everything was very good.  The short rib Koja was sweet and tasty.  The rice "buns" were a bit strange.  They are crispy and work well with the meat but they kinda have the texture of the burnt rice at the bottom of the rice cooker.  The taco and fries were also good.

About the only bad thing I can say about the place is the prices.  I think the prices are a bit high for what you get.< /review>< pictures>

< review>
It's amusing that people who come here lament that this place is expensive, but given that this foodie chain originated in San Francisco, Koja Kitchen is a relatively affordable affair--at least next to the artisan, organic, hand-crafted, etc. foods and wares of the city. This place delivers the same fabulous crispy rice burgers in a nice la, modern, polished setting, a welcome addition in a bright corner of a suburban plaza that houses a few other popular fast-ish food chains like Five Guys and Chipotle. I would pick Koja every time.<//review>

< Text>
It's definitely for the younger crowd.

Environment is modern and is made for you to socialize surrounded by 4 big TVs playing sports.  It seems like a lot of fun here on Warriors nights.  Expect a long wait.  Order line goes fast, but the food takes a long time to come out.  They give you a buzzer to pick up your food.  Everyone here seems to be in their Teens to Mid 20s.

Service is friendly and efficient.

The food is VERY tasty.  I tried the short rib koja, braised pork bowl, and the beef taco.  I recommend the bowl since it comes with a decent amount of salad and rice to balance out the over marinated meat.</Text>

<Date>1450586510828</Date><rating>4< /rating><text>I remember Koja Kitchen was serving rice burgers in food truck before in various events and now finally opened their own restaurant.
The place replaced the previous 'whisper cafe' which specializes in crepe.

<user_name>Kimberly Ann Graham</user_name>< Time>
1458710751787<//Time>
< rating>
4</rating>
< Review>
Sushi Rice makes amazing buns!

Their Koja sandwiches involve different Korean influenced proteins on Sushi Rice buns that have been crisped on the flat top grill.  The flavors are intense, running from sweet (beef kalbi) to the tart of kimchi or the creamy of Japanese Mayo.  Drizzle some red sauce (hot!) over the whole thing and you've got a party in your mouth.  The Kamikaze Fries are all of those ingredients on top of criss-cut waffle fries.  I also tried their Strawberry Mango Lemonade, very refreshing and not overly sweet.

This would probably be a 5 star except for the Short Rib on the Koja was just a little bit too chewy.  Little more time in the marinade maybe.  I'll definitely go back so we'll see.<//Review>

Tanay Gavankar< /name>

<UserId.>108228920550496655772< /UserId.>< text>
I've had their foodtruck once when they came to my office, and I really liked it. I was super hyped to hear that they opened a branch here, and definitely had to try it out. First off, it's SUPER busy near any meal (as in, wait for 45 minutes to place your order). This may have changed recently, but just keep that in mind. I went on a Friday at 2:30pm and ordered in minutes, and got my food in another 5 minutes - very fast service. It was still quite busy (90% of the tables were full), which is a testament to the quality of the food for it being such a weird time.

I had the shortrib Koja and the kamikaze fries. I really liked the koja (the rice-bread was crispy on the outside and soft/sticky on the inside, awesome!), but the shortrib wasn't great. The flavor of the meat and marinade was good, but the texture didn't really fit inside of a sandwich. I'll try the bulgogi one next time. I enjoyed the kamikaze fries; I definitely recommend it.

I will be going back, but only during off-hours.< /text>
